# Deep Learning with TensorFlow: Insights and Innovations

> As the AI landscape continuously evolves, understanding the foundational and emerging aspects of deep learning becomes crucial for professionals looking to stay ahead in tech-related fields. This course helps to bridge that gap by offering updated insights on how to leverage the power of TensorFlow applications. Discover the latest features and best practices of TensorFlow with practical applicati

#### Setting up TensorFlow with Codespaces
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/setting-up-tensorflow-with-codespaces?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript

>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/setting-up-tensorflow-with-codespaces?u=76281980&t=8)** So the beauty of Codespaces is that it automatically configures your environment, thanks to the requirements.txt file included in the course repository.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/setting-up-tensorflow-with-codespaces?u=76281980&t=18)** So here, I have placed the requirements.txt file under the src folder.

> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/setting-up-tensorflow-with-codespaces?u=76281980&t=23)** So let's go ahead and expand the src folder.

> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/setting-up-tensorflow-with-codespaces?u=76281980&t=26)** Scroll down and then you will see the requirements.txt file.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/setting-up-tensorflow-with-codespaces?u=76281980&t=31)** So once you create or open your codespace, the setup process will begin automatically.
>

> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/setting-up-tensorflow-with-codespaces?u=76281980&t=63)** Whether you are running your code directly in the browser-based editor, like we have open right now, or in Visual Studio Code on your desktop by clicking the left pane on the Codespaces and then choosing Open VS Code Desktop, and then it will give you a prompt and it will say you can close this web browser right now.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/setting-up-tensorflow-with-codespaces?u=76281980&t=83)** And you are going to go ahead and extend GitHub Codespaces to open this URI.

> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/setting-up-tensorflow-with-codespaces?u=76281980&t=89)** So regardless of your environment, whether it's web or the desktop version, your development environment will be fully equipped to handle all TensorFlow-related tasks.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/setting-up-tensorflow-with-codespaces?u=76281980&t=101)** So no need to worry about manual installations or configuration hiccups.

### 2. Understanding TensorFlow

#### TensorFlow essentials
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In this session, we are going to explore how you can become a master chef in the world of neural networks using TensorFlow.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=9)** Think of Keras as your sauce chef, making things easier.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=12)** But we are also going to dive into the kitchen ourselves and get our hands dirty with TensorFlow's lower-level API for more control and customization.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=24)** Why use TensorFlow's lower-level API?
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=28)** Think of Keras as your sauce chef, handling the basics so you can focus on creating great recipes or deep learning models.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=37)** Keras simplifies model building, but sometimes you need more control, like adding a secret ingredient or adjusting the cooking time.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=46)** This API allows you to write custom loss functions, metrics, initializers, and more.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=53)** So think of it as like having the freedom to tweak every aspect of your dish to perfection.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=60)** So let's go over and do a quick tour of TensorFlow.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=64)** So think of TensorFlow as like a high-powered kitchen appliance, versatile and efficient for numerical computations and machine learning tasks.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=74)** It's developed by Google's Brain Team.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=78)** It's the secret sauce behind many of Google's services, like Google Photos and search.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=82)** So TensorFlow has become a staple in the deep learning community, much like a go-to cookbook in a chef's kitchen.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=90)** So what are some of TensorFlow's futures?
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=93)** First of all, similarity to NumPy.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=96)** If you have used the Python library NumPy, TensorFlow will feel familiar, but with the added power of GPU support.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=104)** So keep in mind at the time of this recording, codespaces do not support GPU.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=109)** So for the sake of this class, we won't be utilizing GPU, but just know that if you are utilizing TensorFlow in your local environment, and if you do have access to a GPU support, TensorFlow is very similar to NumPy with added GPU support.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=125)** So imagine NumPy as your basic kitchen tools and TensorFlow as those same tools with turbo boosts.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=133)** Let's talk about distributed computing.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=135)** It's like having multiple cooks in the kitchen, each handling different tasks simultaneously across multiple devices.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=144)** This ensures your complex meal or your deep learning model gets done faster and more efficiently.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-essentials?u=76281980&t=151)** So let's look at just-in-time compiler next.
>

#### TensorFlow simplified for NumPy users
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In this session, we will explore how to use TensorFlow like NumPy.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=5)** TensorFlow's API revolves around tensors, which are essentially multi-dimensional arrays similar to NumPy's ndarray.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=14)** These tensors are crucial for creating custom cost functions, metrics, custom layers and more.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=22)** You can create a tensor using tf.constant.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=25)** For example, tf.constant, and then you insert the elements of the tensor.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=31)** This creates a 2x3 matrix of floats.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=34)** Scalars can also be created like tf.constant and you input the scaler, like 42 in our case.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=42)** Tensors have properties such as shape and data type, which you can access using t.shape and t.dtype.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=50)** Indexing tensors works much like NumPy.

> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=63)** So this defines which part of the tensor you would like to access to using the indexing function.

> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=69)** Tensor operations are also very straightforward, such as adding 10 to a tensor, t plus 10.

> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=76)** This is equivalent to using tf.n t comma 10.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=81)** Other operations like tf.square and tf.transpose are also available.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=87)** TensorFlow provides all the basic math operations you need, such as tf.add, tf.multiply, and tf.square.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=97)** These are equivalent to NumPy functions like np.add and np.sum.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=103)** So there are some key differences we should be pointing out here.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=107)** For example, transposing a tensor requires tf.transpose instead of t.T in NumPy.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=116)** Additionally, TensorFlows reduce operations like tf.reduce_sum and tf.reduce_max may have slight variations in precision compared to NumPy.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=129)** Keras also has a low level API located in keras.backend.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=135)** Functions like square, exp and sqrt are available.

>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=145)** If you want your code to be portable across Keras implementations, use these functions.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=150)** For example, using Keras' backend, you can write k.square (K.transpose(t)) + 10.

> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/tensorflow-simplified-for-numpy-users?u=76281980&t=161)** Tensors play nicely with Numpy.

> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/machine-learning-workflow?u=76281980&t=107)** In our example, we will use the California housing prices dataset based on the 1990 California census.

>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/machine-learning-workflow?u=76281980&t=187)** Categorical data needs encoding, which can be done using OrdinalEncoder or OneHotEncoder.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/machine-learning-workflow?u=76281980&t=195)** Categorical encoding is nothing but a fancy way of saying changing the labels and categories into numbers, which machine learning algorithms can understand.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/machine-learning-workflow?u=76281980&t=205)** Future scaling ensures all numerical attributes are on the same scale, using tools like StandardScaler.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/machine-learning-workflow?u=76281980&t=213)** Therefore, if we have a relatively huge number and we have a very small number, those differences does not impact the machine learning algorithm negatively.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/machine-learning-workflow?u=76281980&t=224)** This preparation sets the stage for effective machine learning, like marinating the meat or chopping vegetables before cooking.

>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=121)** So, for that we can remove the task and hint from the challenge and start normalizing it.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=126)** So, normalized_tensor will be, in this case, equal to tensor divided by 9.0.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=138)** So, to normalize the tensor we divide all elements by the maximum value in our original range, which was 9.0.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=147)** So, after taking care of that we can now compute the mean and the standard deviation as they were asked from us in the challenge.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=156)** So, let's go ahead and take care of those by using TensorFlow built-in functions.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=162)** So, we are going to go ahead and start with mean.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=166)** So, we will remove the task here and compute the mean and standard deviation of the normalized tensor.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=173)** So, to do that we will use a built-in function called tf.reduce_mean, and then we will give the normalized tensor as a input.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=185)** And done, we took care of the calculation of the mean.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=189)** Now, next we will go ahead and calculate the standard deviation.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=193)** So, this was compute the mean of the normalized tensor, and this is the compute the standard deviation of the normalized tensor next.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=205)** So, let's go ahead and do that.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=209)** And again, we will use a built-in function for that, so standard deviation will be equal to tf.math.reduce_std.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=223)** So, this will give us the standard deviation, and we will input the normalized tensor here.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-step-by-step-statistical-analysis?u=76281980&t=230)** So, that's it, it will take care of our solution.

>
> **[13:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/autoencoders-a-gentle-introduction-to-generative-models?u=76281980&t=828)** So what can we say to conclude about autoencoder step?
>
> **[13:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/autoencoders-a-gentle-introduction-to-generative-models?u=76281980&t=832)** So this autoencoder model was successful.
>
> **[13:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/autoencoders-a-gentle-introduction-to-generative-models?u=76281980&t=836)** It trained successfully to reconstruct the input data and the results show a reasonable construction capability, especially for the training data.
>
> **[14:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/autoencoders-a-gentle-introduction-to-generative-models?u=76281980&t=846)** The discrepancy in validation loss indicates that the model might not generalize well, especially to unseen data.
>
> **[14:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/autoencoders-a-gentle-introduction-to-generative-models?u=76281980&t=855)** It suggests that we might want to consider some further tuning, or we might consider a more complex model in order to improve the performance.
>
> **[14:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/autoencoders-a-gentle-introduction-to-generative-models?u=76281980&t=865)** When we look at the reconstruction plots, they visually confirm that while the model captures the general trend of the data, there are still small errors in the reconstruction and they are particularly noticeable in the validation set.
>
> **[14:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/autoencoders-a-gentle-introduction-to-generative-models?u=76281980&t=882)** So to conclude, we can say that autoencoders are a type of neural network designed to learn efficient representation of data, typically for the purpose of dimensionality reduction.
>
> **[14:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/autoencoders-a-gentle-introduction-to-generative-models?u=76281980&t=895)** The key behind this is that it tries to learn an encoding, in other words, a compressed representation of the input data and then reconstructs the input from its encoding.
>
> **[15:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/autoencoders-a-gentle-introduction-to-generative-models?u=76281980&t=907)** So that wraps up our encoding session.

> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=84)** Next we are going to fit transform the X train data by calling scaler.fit_transform, and then we are going to call X_train.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=95)** Next, we are going to transform X validation.

> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=99)** Notice we are not using the fit transform rather we are using the transform only for X validation.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=105)** So it's scaler.transform, and then it will take the X_valid.

>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=291)** SGD is a straightforward and effective optimizer for training neural networks, particularly suitable for smaller models.

> **[11:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=672)** So this plot shows the training loss, which is the blue line, and validation loss, which is the orange line, over 20 iterations, 20 epochs during the training of a neural network.
>
> **[11:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=686)** What are the key observations we can take away from this plot?
>
> **[11:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=690)** The validation loss starts relatively high and increases significantly within the first few epochs reaching a peak of over 5.
>
> **[11:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=700)** Well, what does it indicate?
>
> **[11:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=701)** This indicates that the model initially struggles to generalize well to the validation data.
>
> **[11:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=709)** The validation loss fluctuates quite a bit in the early epochs with sharp increases and decreases.
>
> **[11:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=716)** So this could suggest that the model is unstable in the beginning, possibly due to the learning rate or random initialization of weights.
>
> **[12:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=726)** Next around epoch 5, we can see that the validation loss experiences a significant drop and then continues to decrease, stabilizing at a much lower level.
>
> **[12:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=739)** Well, what does it suggest?
>
> **[12:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=741)** This suggests that the model eventually learns to generalize better to the validation data.
>
> **[12:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=748)** The training loss decreases smoothly and remains low throughout the training process, indicating that the model is learning the training data consistently without much difficulty.
>
> **[12:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=761)** So by the end of the training, which is after around epoch 7, both the training and validation losses are quite low and relatively stable we can say.
>
> **[12:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=773)** This indicates that the model has learned the patterns in the data and is not overfitting.
>
> **[13:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=780)** So what can we take away from this?
>
> **[13:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=782)** Well, initial instability.
>
> **[13:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=785)** The significant fluctuations in validation loss during the first few epochs suggest that the model initially has difficulty finding a stable solution.
>
> **[13:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=796)** Well, this could be due to various factors such as the learning rate, weight initialization, or even the complexity of our data.
>
> **[13:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=804)** The training loss is consistently lower than the validation loss, which is quite typical, but should be monitored.
>
> **[13:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=812)** However, since the validation loss stabilizes at a low value, there is no strong indication of overfitting here.
>
> **[13:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=820)** Given that the loss values stabilize after a few epochs, we can consider implementing a early stopping criteria in the future.
>
> **[13:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=829)** This would help us avoid unnecessary training beyond this point, and it would save computational resources.
>
> **[13:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=837)** Despite the initial instability, the model eventually generalizes quite well as evidenced by the stable and low validation loss towards the end of the training.
>
> **[14:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/solution-building-blocks-to-tensorflow-mastery?u=76281980&t=849)** So finally, we can say this plot indicates that the model faced challenges in the early stages of training, particularly with generalizing to validation data, but it eventually found a stable solution with both training and validation losses converging to low values.

>
> **[13:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=783)** If the biases are consistently high or low, it might indicate an issue with the learning rate or data distribution.
>

> **[13:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=814)** So why is this important?
>
> **[13:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=816)** Understanding how the learning rate behaves during training is crucial because it influences the speed and stability of learning.
>
> **[13:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=825)** A constant learning rate might be sufficient, but in some cases, we might want to adjust it dynamically.
>

>
> **[14:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=869)** So why is this important?
>
> **[14:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=871)** This is important because it's a key graph for understanding how well our model is learning.
>
> **[14:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=878)** Ideally, both training and validation losses should decrease and converge.
>
> **[14:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=883)** If the validation loss is much higher or stops decreasing, it might indicate overfitting.
>
> **[14:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=890)** So in our case, they are both decreasing and converging.
>
> **[14:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=895)** Next, moving on to evaluation_loss_vs_iterations.

>
> **[15:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=908)** In other words, validation across different iterations.
>
> **[15:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=912)** So the x-axis represents the iterations and the y-axis shows the loss value.
>
> **[15:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=919)** The curve helps us see how the model's performance changes as it continues to evaluate on the validation set.
>
> **[15:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=929)** It's important because it helps us diagnose how stable the model is during evaluation.
>
> **[15:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=935)** If the loss continues to decrease, it means the model is improving.
>
> **[15:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=940)** However, if it fluctuates or starts to increase, we might be seeing signs of overfeeding.
>
> **[15:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=947)** Then finally, let's go ahead and click on the kernel, which shows the kernel/histogram.
>
> **[15:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=954)** This histogram displays the distribution of the kernel.
>
> **[15:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=958)** In other words, weights.
>
> **[16:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=961)** This is showing the weights during the training phase.
>
> **[16:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=964)** So similar to the bias/histogram, the x-axis represents the range of kernel values, and y-axis here is showing the frequency.
>
> **[16:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=974)** The peaks and shape of the histogram can indicate how the weights are being adjusted throughout the training.
>
> **[16:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=982)** Why is this important?
>
> **[16:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=984)** Monitoring kernel weights is crucial for understanding how the model parameters evolve over time.
>
> **[16:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=991)** Significant shifts or patterns might indicate issues like vanishing gradients or improper initialization.
>
> **[16:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=999)** So to summarize what's important here, the Runs panel on the left, it helps compare different training and validation sessions, and we can run and we can select them by clicking on these boxes or deselect them by clicking again.
>
> **[16:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=1015)** Then we went over the bias/histogram, which monitors the distribution of biases in the model.
>
> **[17:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=1021)** We talked about epoch_learning_rate, which shows the learning rate across epochs.
>
> **[17:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=1027)** Then we went over epoch_loss, which tracks training and validation loss over epochs.
>
> **[17:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=1033)** Then we went over evaluation_loss_vs_iterations.
>
> **[17:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=1037)** This evaluates model stability during validation.
>
> **[17:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=1040)** Then finally, we went over kernel/histogram, which observes the evaluation of weights during training.
>
> **[17:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=1048)** So by looking at these graphs, we understand how TensorBoard provides insights into the training process, which makes it easy to diagnose and improve the model performance.
>
> **[17:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/deep-learning-with-tensorflow-insights-and-innovations/deep-dives-into-training-metrics?u=76281980&t=1061)** So in this session, we saw how we can organize our logs into a specific folder, and then how we can see the results from the TensorBoard and how we can evaluate them.
